# NJCAA WOMEN Visual Materials

**Degree Path:** Bachelor of Science in Basketball Officiating - Collegiate Foundation Track
**Academic Level:** Bachelor Year 1 / Associate-to-Bachelor Bridge
**Course Cover:** `frontend/public/assets/images/refzone/course-covers/njcaa-women.svg`

## Course Overview

This track is designed for junior-college women’s basketball officials preparing to manage developing collegiate athletes, diverse gym environments, quick roster turnover, and freedom-of-movement responsibilities. Students in this track study the full annual officiating cycle through classroom lecture, court mechanics, film laboratory, role-play, live practicum, mentoring, written exams, oral defense, and advancement board review. The teaching emphasis throughout the year is to teach fairness, safety, and disciplined communication in the junior-college women’s game.

## Course Image Brief

**Visual Elements:** junior-college women's basketball gym with developing collegiate athletes in motion, perimeter freedom-of-movement coverage, mentor clipboard, whistle, and two-person/three-person mechanics diagram
**Visual Emphasis:** fairness, safety, disciplined communication, quick roster turnover, and junior-college women's game management
**Image Prompt:** Create a RefZone University course-card image for NJCAA WOMEN: junior-college women's basketball gym with developing collegiate athletes in motion, perimeter freedom-of-movement coverage, mentor clipboard, whistle, and two-person/three-person mechanics diagram. Emphasize fairness, safety, disciplined communication, quick roster turnover, and junior-college women's game management. Use a premium basketball officiating education style with black, metallic silver, white, and orange accents, clean readable course title text, dramatic court lighting, and professional academic training energy. Avoid real school logos, real league logos, and recognizable real people.

## Graduation Requirements

- Complete all 52 weeks of daily academic work.
- Pass all written rules and philosophy examinations.
- Complete every film-lab assignment and full-game self-scout.
- Demonstrate mechanics competence in two-person and three-person systems appropriate to the track.
- Complete role-play scenarios involving coaches, players, partners, table crew, observers, and supervisors.
- Submit required reports for technical, flagrant, administrative, spectator, facility, and unusual situations applicable to the track.
- Complete live-practicum observations and receive mentor/evaluator approval.
- Defend final portfolio before the RTBO advancement board.

## Weekly Materials

### Week 1: Orientation and Professional Identity

- Screenshot package: learner screen, week overview, active lesson view, and progress state.
- Presentation source: `docs/refzone-university/presentation-outlines/njcaa-women-presentation.md#week-1`.
- Required evidence: Students must produce a written journal entry, a film-lab worksheet, a court-lab rubric, a role-play score, and a mentor note showing how Orientation and Professional Identity affects the NJCAA Women environment. If a student cannot produce evidence, the week is not complete.
- Day 1: Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar - Professor Lecture; visual `/assets/images/refzone/lesson-visuals/lecture.svg`.
  - Screenshot: `/assets/images/refzone/course-screenshots/njcaa-women-lecture.svg`.
  - Required reading: Read the current NJCAA-adopted college basketball rulebook for this track sections tied to Orientation and Professional Identity; mark definitions, penalties, exceptions, and restart language that affect Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar. Read the current governing case plays, interpretations, and conference bulletins connected to Orientation and Professional Identity; write the ruling, the reason, the crew responsibility, and the best supervisor explanation. Study the current two-person and three-person mechanics manual used by the assigning body for the day's coverage problem; draw the official's starting position, movement path, primary area, secondary awareness, and reporting route. Review junior-college sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, and game-report procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the professor lecture visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar.
  - Assessment: Written Knowledge Check - 80% or mentor approval is required before Day 2 unlocks.
  - Line Item 1 - Professor Explanation: instruction-slide; Professor-facing lecture slide, visual aid, and discussion prompt.
  - Line Item 2 - What the Student Performs: student-activity; Student-facing worksheet, lab action, and participation artifact.
  - Line Item 3 - Expected Outcome, Evidence, and Grading: assessment-evidence; Assessment-facing quiz/test item, rubric row, and evidence checkpoint.

  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Rules, Case Plays, and Written Reasoning.
  - Assessment: Rules Quiz - 80% or mentor approval is required before Day 3 unlocks.
  - Line Item 1 - Professor Explanation: instruction-slide; Professor-facing lecture slide, visual aid, and discussion prompt.

### Week 4: Communication Psychology

- Screenshot package: learner screen, week overview, active lesson view, and progress state.
- Presentation source: `docs/refzone-university/presentation-outlines/njcaa-women-presentation.md#week-4`.
- Required evidence: Students must produce a written journal entry, a film-lab worksheet, a court-lab rubric, a role-play score, and a mentor note showing how Communication Psychology affects the NJCAA Women environment. If a student cannot produce evidence, the week is not complete.

Read the current governing case plays, interpretations, and conference bulletins connected to Technical and Reportable Conduct; write the ruling, the reason, the crew responsibility, and the best supervisor explanation. Study the current two-person and three-person mechanics manual used by the assigning body for the day's coverage problem; draw the official's starting position, movement path, primary area, secondary awareness, and reporting route. Review junior-college sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, and game-report procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the professor lecture visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar.

### Week 9: Two-Person Mechanics Laboratory

- Screenshot package: learner screen, week overview, active lesson view, and progress state.
- Presentation source: `docs/refzone-university/presentation-outlines/njcaa-women-presentation.md#week-9`.
- Required evidence: Students must produce a written journal entry, a film-lab worksheet, a court-lab rubric, a role-play score, and a mentor note showing how Two-Person Mechanics Laboratory affects the NJCAA Women environment. If a student cannot produce evidence, the week is not complete.
- Day 1: Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar - Professor Lecture; visual `/assets/images/refzone/lesson-visuals/lecture.svg`.
  - Screenshot: `/assets/images/refzone/course-screenshots/njcaa-women-lecture.svg`.

Read the current governing case plays, interpretations, and conference bulletins connected to Two-Person Mechanics Laboratory; write the ruling, the reason, the crew responsibility, and the best supervisor explanation. Study the current two-person and three-person mechanics manual used by the assigning body for the day's coverage problem; draw the official's starting position, movement path, primary area, secondary awareness, and reporting route. Review junior-college sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, and game-report procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. ### Week 11: Transition, Press Coverage, and Fast-Break Judgment

- Screenshot package: learner screen, week overview, active lesson view, and progress state.
- Presentation source: `docs/refzone-university/presentation-outlines/njcaa-women-presentation.md#week-11`.
- Required evidence: Students must produce a written journal entry, a film-lab worksheet, a court-lab rubric, a role-play score, and a mentor note showing how Transition, Press Coverage, and Fast-Break Judgment affects the NJCAA Women environment. If a student cannot produce evidence, the week is not complete.

  - Required reading: Read the current NJCAA-adopted college basketball rulebook for this track sections tied to Player Safety and Severe Contact; mark definitions, penalties, exceptions, and restart language that affect Rules, Case Plays, and Written Reasoning. Read the current governing case plays, interpretations, and conference bulletins connected to Player Safety and Severe Contact; write the ruling, the reason, the crew responsibility, and the best supervisor explanation. Study the current two-person and three-person mechanics manual used by the assigning body for the day's coverage problem; draw the official's starting position, movement path, primary area, secondary awareness, and reporting route. Review junior-college sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, and game-report procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the rules and case plays visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Rules, Case Plays, and Written Reasoning.
  - Assessment: Rules Quiz - 80% or mentor approval is required before Day 3 unlocks.

### Week 16: Coach Communication and Bench Control

  - Required reading: Read the current NJCAA-adopted college basketball rulebook for this track sections tied to Player Communication and Preventive Officiating; mark definitions, penalties, exceptions, and restart language that affect Role-Play, Communication, and Oral Defense. Read the current governing case plays, interpretations, and conference bulletins connected to Player Communication and Preventive Officiating; write the ruling, the reason, the crew responsibility, and the best supervisor explanation. Study the current two-person and three-person mechanics manual used by the assigning body for the day's coverage problem; draw the official's starting position, movement path, primary area, secondary awareness, and reporting route. Review junior-college sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, and game-report procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the role-play and oral defense visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.

  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Rules, Case Plays, and Written Reasoning.
  - Assessment: Rules Quiz - 80% or mentor approval is required before Day 3 unlocks.
  - Line Item 1 - Professor Explanation: instruction-slide; Professor-facing lecture slide, visual aid, and discussion prompt.

Study the role-play and oral defense visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Role-Play, Communication, and Oral Defense.
  - Assessment: Video Quiz - 80% or mentor approval is required before Day 6 unlocks.
  - Line Item 1 - Professor Explanation: instruction-slide; Professor-facing lecture slide, visual aid, and discussion prompt.

- Presentation source: `docs/refzone-university/presentation-outlines/njcaa-women-presentation.md#week-32`.
- Required evidence: Students must produce a written journal entry, a film-lab worksheet, a court-lab rubric, a role-play score, and a mentor note showing how Level-Specific Reporting Intensive affects the NJCAA Women environment. If a student cannot produce evidence, the week is not complete.
- Day 1: Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar - Professor Lecture; visual `/assets/images/refzone/lesson-visuals/lecture.svg`.
  - Screenshot: `/assets/images/refzone/course-screenshots/njcaa-women-lecture.svg`.
  - Required reading: Read the current NJCAA-adopted college basketball rulebook for this track sections tied to Level-Specific Reporting Intensive; mark definitions, penalties, exceptions, and restart language that affect Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar. Read the current governing case plays, interpretations, and conference bulletins connected to Level-Specific Reporting Intensive; write the ruling, the reason, the crew responsibility, and the best supervisor explanation. Study the current two-person and three-person mechanics manual used by the assigning body for the day's coverage problem; draw the official's starting position, movement path, primary area, secondary awareness, and reporting route. Review junior-college sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, and game-report procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the professor lecture visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar.
  - Assessment: Written Knowledge Check - 80% or mentor approval is required before Day 2 unlocks.
  - Line Item 1 - Professor Explanation: instruction-slide; Professor-facing lecture slide, visual aid, and discussion prompt.
  - Line Item 2 - What the Student Performs: student-activity; Student-facing worksheet, lab action, and participation artifact.
  - Line Item 3 - Expected Outcome, Evidence, and Grading: assessment-evidence; Assessment-facing quiz/test item, rubric row, and evidence checkpoint.

### Week 35: Report Responsibility and Crew Accountability

- Screenshot package: learner screen, week overview, active lesson view, and progress state.
- Presentation source: `docs/refzone-university/presentation-outlines/njcaa-women-presentation.md#week-35`.
- Required evidence: Students must produce a written journal entry, a film-lab worksheet, a court-lab rubric, a role-play score, and a mentor note showing how Report Responsibility and Crew Accountability affects the NJCAA Women environment. If a student cannot produce evidence, the week is not complete.

  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Rules, Case Plays, and Written Reasoning.
  - Assessment: Rules Quiz - 80% or mentor approval is required before Day 3 unlocks.

  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Role-Play, Communication, and Oral Defense.

Read the current governing case plays, interpretations, and conference bulletins connected to Final Live Evaluation; write the ruling, the reason, the crew responsibility, and the best supervisor explanation. Study the current two-person and three-person mechanics manual used by the assigning body for the day's coverage problem; draw the official's starting position, movement path, primary area, secondary awareness, and reporting route. Review junior-college sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, and game-report procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the reflection and mentor review visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Reflection, Remediation, Mentor Conference, and Advancement Record.

  - Required reading: Read the current NJCAA-adopted college basketball rulebook for this track sections tied to Certification and Placement; mark definitions, penalties, exceptions, and restart language that affect Court Laboratory and Mechanics Performance. Read the current governing case plays, interpretations, and conference bulletins connected to Certification and Placement; write the ruling, the reason, the crew responsibility, and the best supervisor explanation. Study the current two-person and three-person mechanics manual used by the assigning body for the day's coverage problem; draw the official's starting position, movement path, primary area, secondary awareness, and reporting route. Review junior-college sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, and game-report procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the court mechanics lab visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.

### Week 52: Program Reset and Continuing Education

- Screenshot package: learner screen, week overview, active lesson view, and progress state.
- Presentation source: `docs/refzone-university/presentation-outlines/njcaa-women-presentation.md#week-52`.
- Required evidence: Students must produce a written journal entry, a film-lab worksheet, a court-lab rubric, a role-play score, and a mentor note showing how Program Reset and Continuing Education affects the NJCAA Women environment. If a student cannot produce evidence, the week is not complete.
